<div id="review_2748950047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2748950047" />
    <a title="André" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7215128-andr"><img alt="André" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586543083p2/7215128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2748950047?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="André" class="user" itemprop="url" name="André" href="/user/show/7215128-andr">André</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9789895523849" href="/book/show/6326531-o-sonho-dum-homem-rid-culo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7215128-andr?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7215128-andr?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7215128-andr?shelf=literature">literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7215128-andr?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7215128-andr?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2748950047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5118207628187156960"><i>"I will not and cannot believe that evil is the normal condition of mankind."</i><br/><br/><b>The Dream of a Ridiculous Man</b>, written in 1877, is focused on the events of a nameless and nihilistic man that is determined to suicide.<br/>Dostoyevsky presents an insurgent short-story with glimpses of hope towards humankind. <br/><br/>The story starts with the ridiculous man wandering the streets of St. Petersburg with the thought of suicide dwelling in his mind. The narrator feels worthless and apathetic towards humankind, and the</span>
  <span id="freeText5118207628187156960" style="display:none"><i>"I will not and cannot believe that evil is the normal condition of mankind."</i><br /><br /><b>The Dream of a Ridiculous Man</b>, written in 1877, is focused on the events of a nameless and nihilistic man that is determined to suicide.<br />Dostoyevsky presents an insurgent short-story with glimpses of hope towards humankind. <br /><br />The story starts with the ridiculous man wandering the streets of St. Petersburg with the thought of suicide dwelling in his mind. The narrator feels worthless and apathetic towards humankind, and therefore, he plans of shooting himself in the head. In that dreadful night, the ridiculous raconteur sees a lost young girl. He perceives that something is wrong with the girl's mother, careless with her problem, the nameless narrator heads home indifferently. Once at home, the narrator, with his gun beside him, feels guilty about the young girl's situation. As he dwells in internal conflicts and questions, the ridiculous man falls asleep into a lucid dream. <br />The dream starts with a gunshot in the heart committed by the narrator to himself. He feels that our dream sources come from our deepest desires. <br />Buried in a cold grave, the narrator asks for forgiveness and begs for his life. Afterwards, he's transported through space, ending up in a Utopic island. In this island, the inhabitants live peacefully, in collective harmony. Within time, the ridiculous man teaches the inhabitants to lie and to commit other sins. Consequently, the utopic society gets corrupted and damaged. Guilty by his acts, the nameless man blames himself to the inhabitants, telling them to kill him for his actions. The Islanders are indifferent about him and all the current state that the island has turned. <br />The dream message causes a significant result to the narrator.<br /><br />The author presents another figure with an existential crisis. The nameless character desires a sort of utopic society in the real world, but, since he got corrupted by the vile society of the real world, he dreams of corrupting the society in his dream. It's a paradox event that highlights the consequences of society into an ordinary man. He's ridiculous because he feels like an outsider in the real world and with a frustrated desire, a desire about collective harmony and unity that is (almost) impossible to achieve.<br /><br />Rating: 4/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="5118207628187156960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1377404077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1377404077" />
    <a title="Rahil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22368942-rahil"><img alt="Rahil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514741353p2/22368942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3382446753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3382446753" />
    <a title="Manaal Siddiqui" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43679659-manaal-siddiqui"><img alt="Manaal Siddiqui" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592482299p2/43679659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3382446753?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manaal Siddiqui" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manaal Siddiqui" href="/user/show/43679659-manaal-siddiqui">Manaal Siddiqui</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone interested in philosophy, nihilism, thought experiments, and the nature of existence.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3382446753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16690654797898286340">On the surface, Dostoevsky’s “The Dream of a Ridiculous Man” is about the transformation of a man contemplating suicide. The start of the story describes this man’s psychological state of mind— he apparently had a tough childhood and his resulting proud nature might be a coping strategy that helped him survive the ridicule from everyone around him. His pride leads to indifference and thus he reaches the conclusion that his life has no meaning, and subsequently decides to kill himself. However, h</span>
  <span id="freeText16690654797898286340" style="display:none">On the surface, Dostoevsky’s “The Dream of a Ridiculous Man” is about the transformation of a man contemplating suicide. The start of the story describes this man’s psychological state of mind— he apparently had a tough childhood and his resulting proud nature might be a coping strategy that helped him survive the ridicule from everyone around him. His pride leads to indifference and thus he reaches the conclusion that his life has no meaning, and subsequently decides to kill himself. However, he abandons this idea when he has a dream. A dream that plants an idea that completely changes him. The dream reveals his inner nature and we learn that, at its very core, his indifference was a consequence of his life’s troubles rather than a completely intellectual conclusion. <br /><br /> In the process of portraying this man’s transformation, Dostoevsky explores many ideas. His exploration occurs within an account of humanity’s own history: Adam and Eve living in paradise (represent the innocent humans on earth), then Satan misleads them (the dreaming man in this case), causing them to eat the apple (the ridiculous man corrupting humanity), which leads to humanity’s downfall. Dostoevsky highlights humanity’s eternal existential crisis— every person’s constant struggle to find meaning in life, to understand the purpose of their existence. <br /><br />“All are striving in the same direction anyway, from the sage to the lowest robber, only by different roads”<br /><br /> He sets out to prove that nihilism as a thought process is intrinsically flawed. One of the ways he does this is in the form of a thought experiment. <br /><br />“If I had lived before on the moon or on Mars and there had committed the most disgraceful and dishonorable action and had there been put to such shame and ignominy as one can only conceive and realize in dreams, in nightmares, and if, finding myself afterwards on earth, I were able to retain the memory of what I had done on the other planet and at the same time knew that I should never, under any circumstances, return there, then looking from the earth to the moon— should I care or not? Should I feel shame for that action or not?”<br /><br />Dostoevsky, being the genius that he is, indirectly answers this question, and in the process refutes Nietzsche’s attempt to sever connections to a higher order through his struggle against feelings of shame and guilt. The man has a dream (equivalent to going on another planet), and commits the gravest sin of all— he corrupts all of mankind, and is the reason for their downfall. When he wakes up (comes back to Earth) he is shaken to the core by his experience and is forever changed as a person. Thus, counter to nihilistic thought, Dostoevsky proves that man can never escape feelings of guilt and shame. <br /><br />Overall, I loved this book because the ridiculous man taught me that one does not need complicated theories of existence in order to be happy or live a meaningful life. He taught me to be content with life as it is, and to avoid a constant preoccupation with rationalizing the nature of existence and consciousness. <br /><br />“The consciousness of life is higher than life, the knowledge of the laws of happiness is higher than happiness— that is what one must content against.”<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone interested in philosophy, nihilism, thought experiments, and the nature of existence.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16690654797898286340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9nvvTzMwnD+La+bMN3peLzg1AzyZcUneXNiBgDgol40RXMqlvO8S1XR0EGSblsclkTeTq8zVfySAYejEonThkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZSBrFH3XC5BRPFWPY6lMLjQhfUWIcZdlxAqTNuq8pH+CB07+8giFeq4joyfPRdUknSPt0t3VoZ8Ys/pycODSYg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3137322.Fyodor_Dostoyevsky">About Fyodor Dostoyevsky</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3137322.Fyodor_Dostoyevsky"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1506003555p3/3137322.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3137322.Fyodor_Dostoyevsky">Fyodor Dostoyevsky
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
35,910
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3200213175772478897">Fyodor Mikhailovich Dostoevsky was born in Moscow in 1821. His debut, the epistolary novella Poor Folk (1846), made his name. In 1849 he was arrested for involvement with the politically subversive 'Petrashevsky circle' and until 1854 he lived in a convict prison in Omsk, Siberia. From this experience came The House of the Dead (1860-2). In 1860 he began the journal Vremya (Time). Already married,</span>
  <span id="freeText3200213175772478897" style="display:none">Fyodor Mikhailovich Dostoevsky was born in Moscow in 1821. His debut, the epistolary novella Poor Folk (1846), made his name. In 1849 he was arrested for involvement with the politically subversive 'Petrashevsky circle' and until 1854 he lived in a convict prison in Omsk, Siberia. From this experience came The House of the Dead (1860-2). In 1860 he began the journal Vremya (Time). Already married, he fell in love with one of his contributors, Appollinaria Suslova, eighteen years his junior, and developed a ruinous passion for roulette. After the death of his first wife, Maria, in 1864, Dostoyevsky completed Notes from Underground and began work towards Crime and Punishment (1866). The major novels of his late period are The Idiot (1868), Demons (1871-2) and The Brothers Karamazov (1879-80). He died in 1881.<br /><br />(Russian: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16321565.____________________________" title="Фёдор Михайлович Достоевский" rel="nofollow noopener">Фёдор Михайлович Достоевский</a>) (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17062424.Fiodor_Dosto_evski" title="Fiodor Dostoïevski" rel="nofollow noopener">Fiodor Dostoïevski</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18606930.Fi_dor_M__Dostoievski" title="Fiódor M. Dostoievski" rel="nofollow noopener">Fiódor M. Dostoievski</a>).</span>
  <a data-text-id="3200213175772478897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
